  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f65891ec-6818-489a-9c61-8e3959e11776'
      });
    }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_2450345').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_2450345').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_2450345').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24580404?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/1240712-amber">Amber</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">margie</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24580404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6837480739826342349">I read every one of these books I could find in the library in elementary school and junior high. Trashy yet enthralling. I associate them with the period of time I was convinced I could have superpowers if only I tried hard enough. I really really wanted paranormal powers-- particularly telekinesis. If it could happen to the girls in these books.. why not me?</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2488853024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2488853024" />
    <a title="Ken" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38999260-ken"><img alt="Ken" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446483502p2/38999260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2488853024?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ken" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ken" href="/user/show/38999260-ken">Ken</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316099042" href="/book/show/9543660-stranger-with-my-face">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2488853024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer120919984843031151">As ‘Teen Creeps Podcast’ are covering this book, I wanted to read it before the latest episode was released.<br/>This is my first Lois Duncan novel, though I know they covered some of her other books. I’m slowly working through the back catalogue!<br/><br/>Laurie’s friends and family keep telling her that they have seen her in places where she can’t have been, as Laurie was ill in bed. So how is this mysterious stranger?<br/>I really liked the set up to the story, it’s a great mystery that instantly hooked me in.<br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText120919984843031151" style="display:none">As ‘Teen Creeps Podcast’ are covering this book, I wanted to read it before the latest episode was released.<br />This is my first Lois Duncan novel, though I know they covered some of her other books. I’m slowly working through the back catalogue!<br /><br />Laurie’s friends and family keep telling her that they have seen her in places where she can’t have been, as Laurie was ill in bed. So how is this mysterious stranger?<br />I really liked the set up to the story, it’s a great mystery that instantly hooked me in.<br />I was slightly disappointed when it was revealed early on the stranger is Laurie’s twin and that they had both been adopted.<br />I was really enjoying that element of the story.<br /><br />Laurie is then introduced to astral projection and the story takes a great creepy turn.<br />I really had fun reading this, the narrative flowed quickly and I enjoyed Duncan’s style of writing.<br />I’m looking forward to reading more of her work.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="120919984843031151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780812402001" href="/book/show/9280615-stranger-with-my-face">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2013-challenge">2013-challenge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662406575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5677528725366573816">This was a pretty good tale, and the first time for me to read anything from Lois Duncan. I have become intrigued with this Authors talent, and plan on reading more of her works in the future. <br/><br/>No the book did not blow me away, but it was still very well written. The story was very fluid and easy to read and follow. I was a bit confused at the ending and felt like I was left hanging a bit, like it seemed to be left open for a sequel, but I would have liked a little more closure though.<br/><br/>Our main ch</span>
  <span id="freeText5677528725366573816" style="display:none">This was a pretty good tale, and the first time for me to read anything from Lois Duncan. I have become intrigued with this Authors talent, and plan on reading more of her works in the future. <br /><br />No the book did not blow me away, but it was still very well written. The story was very fluid and easy to read and follow. I was a bit confused at the ending and felt like I was left hanging a bit, like it seemed to be left open for a sequel, but I would have liked a little more closure though.<br /><br />Our main character, Laurie, was probably the strongest and best developed in the book, I loved her determination and courage. Her parents were not likable at all for me though, They were so close minded throughout the entire story. I could not imagine not even listening to my kids when they were distressed about something. It was like they did not wanna deal with problems that were brought into the story, wanted to act like nothing was wrong at all.<br /><br />I thought the premise of the book was great, loved the idea. I would liked to have seen a bit more work put into it though. I feel as though the story could be so much more than it was, kinda fell a little short. This could have easily been a 300 - 350 page novel. This book gets a 3.5 rating from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5677528725366573816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I may have the details wrong about who the girl who slips into the body is. In any case, the protagonist is floating around in spirit, watching some othe</span>
  <span id="freeText14546747580953714518" style="display:none">I read this book years and years ago. In fact, I wasn't sure I had actually read it until I saw the summary of it in <i>Bitch</i> magazine.<br /><br />It's a really creepy premise. A teenage girl is doing astral projection and while she's out of her body, the sister she didn't know she had slips <i>her</i> spirit into the vacated body. Well, something like that happens. I may have the details wrong about who the girl who slips into the body is. In any case, the protagonist is floating around in spirit, watching some other spirit propelling her body around. Of course, everyone thinks the protagonist's body is inhabited by the protagonist's spirit, and there's not much she can do to correct the mistake.<br /><br />Kept me too scared to try astral projection during the time I thought it was maybe possible.</span>

  <span id="freeText15549029570559115301" style="display:none">I haven't read this book in a very long time. But I first discovered it when I was probably 10-years-old and I just kept taking it out of the library! I knew exactly where it was, what shelf it was on and it was ALWAYS there waiting for me. The librarians used to look at me and say, "Well there you go again Paula." This was my first introduction to science fiction (at least in book form) and it was awesome! What if your friends suddenly started acting strange and told you you did things that you don't remember? What if you started seeing strange things through your own eyes? This book is creepy, but a real page turner.</span>

    <a title="Amanda " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4929450-amanda"><img alt="Amanda " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596561033p2/4929450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2985758901?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda " href="/user/show/4929450-amanda">Amanda </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316099042" href="/book/show/9543660-stranger-with-my-face">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2985758901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13492382435203692608">This wasn't my first Lois Duncan but it will probably be my last. Duncan's writing is dated and simplistic by today's YA standards. It just doesn't seem to cut it for more reasons than one.<br/><br/>The story was published in 1981 and it was very clear exactly where the author added updates. Not many teens would call a boyfriend's cell and then try calling the boyfriend's dad (many people no longer have landlines nor know the number of a friend's parent). Calling a parent Mother or younger siblings The Ch</span>
  <span id="freeText13492382435203692608" style="display:none">This wasn't my first Lois Duncan but it will probably be my last. Duncan's writing is dated and simplistic by today's YA standards. It just doesn't seem to cut it for more reasons than one.<br /><br />The story was published in 1981 and it was very clear exactly where the author added updates. Not many teens would call a boyfriend's cell and then try calling the boyfriend's dad (many people no longer have landlines nor know the number of a friend's parent). Calling a parent Mother or younger siblings The Children, or having a writer father use a typewriter set this novel firmly in the past and leaves the reader with an odd disconnect as well as a reminder of how much technology has transformed everyone's daily lives.<br /><br />The whole premise of the book, that new age astral projection is real and that it is somehow tied to Navajo beliefs is both laughable and an outdated and insensitive stereotype. The fact that Duncan claims to have experienced it herself occasionally in an author's interview at the end made me question her grasp on reality.<br /><br />Duncan's stories seem on par with the ability of a middle school writer. I wouldn't recommend them for anyone above eighth grade.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13492382435203692608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162113307?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/5289798-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">suspense readers and writers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289798-lena?shelf=love-of-learning">love-of-learning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5289798-lena?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162113307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10927380545540231559">I didn't know what to expect when I got this book from the library. I had heard of the author, but I'd never read anything by her. <br/><br/>Duncan does an amazing job creating suspense. It was SO HARD to put this book down every time I had to stop reading. It caught me and never let go--the pace is relentless. This should be required reading for suspense writers, because so many get it wrong. Duncan is a master. <br/><br/>That said, I didn't really care for the main character. I tried hard to like her, and succeed</span>
  <span id="freeText10927380545540231559" style="display:none">I didn't know what to expect when I got this book from the library. I had heard of the author, but I'd never read anything by her. <br /><br />Duncan does an amazing job creating suspense. It was SO HARD to put this book down every time I had to stop reading. It caught me and never let go--the pace is relentless. This should be required reading for suspense writers, because so many get it wrong. Duncan is a master. <br /><br />That said, I didn't really care for the main character. I tried hard to like her, and succeeded only partially. I did have sympathy for her, but some of her decisions were just so stupid it made things harder. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Like, how did she NOT know Leah was evil? I knew the second Leah tried to get her to leave her body that Leah was going to steal it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And I found parts of the book way too predictible for a suspense novel.<br /><br />Overall, though, I did enjoy this book. It was very well crafted. A little less foreshadowing would have made me like it more. Also, the whole thing with the boy with the damaged face really added interest to the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ For some reason I didn't really believe in the relationship between the protagonist and the boy with the messed up face, though. It just happened so suddenly I was like "WHAT? Since when? Come on, make me believe it a little more than that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I liked how the ending was good, but not all shiny happy, either.<br /><br />Fun, interesting, absorbing read. Very exciting and suspenseful.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10927380545540231559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2446766914560649331" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars.</b><br /><br /><i>”Are you the one with my face?” I whispered. <br />“I came first.” She answered with a little laugh. “It’s you who has my face.”</i><br /><br />I can see why this book was such a big hit back in the early 90’s. <div id="review_187109265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187109265" />
    <a title="Midnyte Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3726186-midnyte-reader"><img alt="Midnyte Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277160269p2/3726186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187109265?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Midnyte Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Midnyte Reader" href="/user/show/3726186-midnyte-reader">Midnyte Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3726186-midnyte-reader?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3726186-midnyte-reader?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187109265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer901584175395352515">Lois Duncan is a huge name in the literary world, who has written many, (many, many) books and received many (manymanymany) awards. I Know What You Did Last Summer may be her most recognizable. However, I can't remember reading any of her books growing up, but I recognized her name when I picked up this audio book in the library. My other reasons for checking this out were 1) We don't have a huge selection in our library and 2) It was earmarked as Supernatural. I'm not sure I would really recomm</span>
  <span id="freeText901584175395352515" style="display:none">Lois Duncan is a huge name in the literary world, who has written many, (many, many) books and received many (manymanymany) awards. I Know What You Did Last Summer may be her most recognizable. However, I can't remember reading any of her books growing up, but I recognized her name when I picked up this audio book in the library. My other reasons for checking this out were 1) We don't have a huge selection in our library and 2) It was earmarked as Supernatural. I'm not sure I would really recommend it, but it did win a ton of awards. <br /><br />The story was published in 1981 and yes, the book is a bit dated. Not just because the father who is a writer uses a typewriter, but it just didn’t have a contemporary feel. However, the story holds up and the plot is fun. Although it is a bit predictable, I didn’t know everything that was going to happen and I do like how it was all resolved. <br /><br />I didn’t really connect to any of the characters, I felt they were kind of stereotyped. The boyfriend who is Mr. Perfect and a tad arrogant, the bad boy who is sullen and most of Laurie's friends who happened to be in the popular crowd. Laurie is nice and perhaps a typical teenager. Her reaction to her parent's secret is understandable but her continuing anger had me a little annoyed.<br /><br />It took me a while to get into the tone of voice of the narrator. At first I felt as if she was reading a bit too deliberately and it just sounded funny. But I did get used to it. <br /><br />Some of the writing sounded odd to me. I’m sure it is correct and I’m not a Grammer expert, but she kept using sentences, like “We, both of us saw you.” “We, none of us…” or “We, all of us…” It just stuck out. I also thought it kind of odd that the main character Lori, who is 17, calls her younger siblings who are 8 and 11 “the children.” I don’t know, maybe it’s because that’s what her parents call them. Also, the issue of adoption is pretty dated. It kind of had me laughing.<br /><br />I think this book would appeal more to middle grade students than young adults. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="901584175395352515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2754841809" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2754841809" />
    <a title="Knobby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9116036-knobby"><img alt="Knobby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350062174p2/9116036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2754841809?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Knobby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Knobby" href="/user/show/9116036-knobby">Knobby</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2754841809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1925141052172301882">Another Lois Duncan from my past... <br/><br/>Like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/522686.The_Third_Eye' title='The Third Eye by Lois Duncan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Third Eye</a>, Stranger With My Face was one of those books I read as a teen. It's suspenseful without thrill, and scary without gore — perfect for me! Laurie lives on Brighton Island in New England with her family, and has a generally normal life. When her boyfriend claims he sees Laurie standing on the beach when she was actually at home with the stomach flu, Laurie is perplexed. More and more of her classmates see "Laurie," and even her little sister M</span>
  <span id="freeText1925141052172301882" style="display:none">Another Lois Duncan from my past... <br /><br />Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/522686.The_Third_Eye" title="The Third Eye by Lois Duncan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Third Eye</a>, Stranger With My Face was one of those books I read as a teen. It's suspenseful without thrill, and scary without gore — perfect for me! Laurie lives on Brighton Island in New England with her family, and has a generally normal life. When her boyfriend claims he sees Laurie standing on the beach when she was actually at home with the stomach flu, Laurie is perplexed. More and more of her classmates see "Laurie," and even her little sister Meg sees Laurie's "ghosty." Everyone who tries to protect Laurie from the mirror girl falls into danger, and Laurie herself is threatened by her double. Who is this girl and what does she want?<br /><br />Even though I read this years ago, I still remember tons of details and enjoyed revisiting it. Lois Duncan is a master at subtle creepiness that stays with you. The scenes where Laurie brushes her hair while looking into a reflection, and then realizing later that her mirror had been smiling but she had not, was a mental image that stuck with me. The description of Laurie learning how to project from her body, too, remained with me for a long time.<br /><br />While Duncan was a master at pacing and having her characters experience confusion or fear, she can't write love worth shit. In The Third Eye, the MC falls for someone in days — might be understandable, given that they were thrust into stressful situations together multiple times. Like Keanu and Sandy in SPEED, sometimes heightened emotions from stress can bring about some kind of lust. But Laurie is as lustful towards her love interest as a wet noodle. I wish her characters could just have strong platonic friendships with guys instead. Ah well. Product of the times.<br /><br />Though the book was updated for newer audiences (the original story was written in the early 1980s), the idea of isolation and spotty cell service makes sense on the tiny Brighton Island where Laurie and her family live. I'm glad that Duncan didn't try to shoehorn Google into the conversation; Laurie reading rare books about astral projection seemed believable enough to me even now.<br /><br />Jenny Han (of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15749186.To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before__To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before___1_" title="To All the Boys I've Loved Before (To All the Boys I've Loved Before, #1) by Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">To All the Boys I've Loved Before</a>) interviews Lois Duncan in the updated version of this book, which I liked. I'm kind of curious who all interviewed Duncan in all of the other updated books of hers. It seems like the who's who of the YA world are involved in the book updates.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1925141052172301882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2298187797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298187797" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58727591-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2298187797?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/58727591-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298187797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8670706591517110394">Rachel Wargo <br/>2/16/18<br/>AP Lang <br/>Mrs. Smeenk<br/>Book Review <br/><br/>		Stranger With My Face is an amazing novel that i would surely recommend for many of my friends. This is a typical mystery novel that is exactly what the title is. This girl, Laurie has her life all put together. She has her siblings, and her great parents. She has her group of friends and the popular guy finally has a crush on her. As she goes through her daily life she doesn’t think anything could go wrong, until another her began to appear. </span>
  <span id="freeText8670706591517110394" style="display:none">Rachel Wargo <br />2/16/18<br />AP Lang <br />Mrs. Smeenk<br />Book Review <br /><br />		Stranger With My Face is an amazing novel that i would surely recommend for many of my friends. This is a typical mystery novel that is exactly what the title is. This girl, Laurie has her life all put together. She has her siblings, and her great parents. She has her group of friends and the popular guy finally has a crush on her. As she goes through her daily life she doesn’t think anything could go wrong, until another her began to appear. In strange places she would see the back of her, her friends were now thinking that Laurie was another person. So many people saw a different Laurie, but nobody knew that there was two of them. Even though there were two of the same characters they still did have their differences. The author, Lois Duncan had an amazing way of showing the unique characteristics of each character. The strict parents who never let Laurie have her fun, her annoying little sister, and Laurie who was an unique individual herself. I got a lot out of each character and i think that is important out of a great novel. This novel is not like any other novel i have read. It was something very different. Because they took this girls life who was such a happy individual and she had everything put together, and just in seconds her life had been changed. She was now on a mission to see who this girl was that was going around pretending to be her. She was slowly taking this girls life away from her, and ruining this life that was made for her. This book also is very suspenseful. It was a story that i did not want to put down and i had to keep reading to see what would happen next. I would suggest this book to any age. I think it’s a easy read, but very entertaining for the reader. And i would say that most people could find it cheesy, but it is interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8670706591517110394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2298187797">

<div id="review_737711022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/737711022" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593071-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356879093p2/4593071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/737711022?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/4593071-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316099042" href="/book/show/9543660-stranger-with-my-face">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10097292-emma-williams">Emma Williams</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593071-anna?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593071-anna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer737711022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14116709132632230905">While discussing the state of popular YA fiction, I was recommended this book by Emma C. Williams, author of 'World Enough and Time'. I pretty much straight away reserved a copy at my local library and after waiting several weeks for it to be ordered in, brought it home and started straight away. I read this in what probably amounts to a 24 hour period. I started it in the evening and finished it the following afternoon. I was just that hooked on it.<br/><br/>Laurie Stratton is just your everyday sixteen </span>
  <span id="freeText14116709132632230905" style="display:none">While discussing the state of popular YA fiction, I was recommended this book by Emma C. Williams, author of 'World Enough and Time'. I pretty much straight away reserved a copy at my local library and after waiting several weeks for it to be ordered in, brought it home and started straight away. I read this in what probably amounts to a 24 hour period. I started it in the evening and finished it the following afternoon. I was just that hooked on it.<br /><br />Laurie Stratton is just your everyday sixteen year old. Over the summer holidays she's gone from lonely geek girl to member of the popular group, dating the school's main jock. So of course, she can't wait for school to start again. But something strange is happening. Her boyfriend and her friends keep saying they've seen her in places she knows she hasn't been and she's sure someone has been in her bedroom and that someone has begun visiting her in her dreams. And then there's the ghost girl her little sister has seen looking in through the windows. What does it all mean?<br /><br />This was a great novel, with a brilliant mystery plot running through it and just the right amount of supernatural elements. The one thing I did find a little bizarre at first was the fact that this novel, which was originally published in the 80s, suddenly had references to mobile phones, laptops and DVD players. And then I twigged that Lois Duncan's novels have all been re-released in a newly edited version up-dating them for the modern teen. It's a clever idea. I remember reading some of her books as a young teenager back in the 90s and the description of teenage life not seeming too alien but I can imagine that todays teenagers might feel differently. They're used to a world where they are surgically attached to their mobile phones and iPads. Getting Lois Duncan to up-date her novels is a brilliant marketing move and it works well. None of the additions seem out of place, it all flows seamlessly.<br /><br />This was a quick, fun read and really took me back to the kind of books I used to read and love as a teenager. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14116709132632230905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2352823697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352823697" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72783771-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508607779p2/72783771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352823697?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/72783771-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316175616" href="/book/show/10515001-stranger-with-my-face">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352823697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14466856029357347573">I read this book because it was chosen by the BookStore podcast and it was short enough to finish before their discussion. The podcast hosts chose it because they had read her books back when they were teens and wanted to reread one of Duncan's books to see how well it held up. Since I am older than they are I hadn't heard of Duncan but have since found out she was a very prolific and popular author among young readers. I enjoyed this book for what it was, an enjoyable suspense/paranormal novel </span>
  <span id="freeText14466856029357347573" style="display:none">I read this book because it was chosen by the BookStore podcast and it was short enough to finish before their discussion. The podcast hosts chose it because they had read her books back when they were teens and wanted to reread one of Duncan's books to see how well it held up. Since I am older than they are I hadn't heard of Duncan but have since found out she was a very prolific and popular author among young readers. I enjoyed this book for what it was, an enjoyable suspense/paranormal novel geared to young adults. It is short and entertaining. The main character is Laurie Stratton. She lives with her parents and two younger sibling in a large cliff-side house on an island. Her parents are artists and somewhat isolated from the rest of the town living on the mainland. Laurie is a senior in high school ready to go back to class for the first day of the new school year. She has spent the previous day with a 24-hour type virus and was not able to attend a party with her boyfriend. He accuses her of lying, saying he saw her on the beach that night with another boy. This sets off a series of events in which people claim they see Laurie when she knows it was not actually her they saw. So it seems there must be someone else that looks just like her. Laurie's discovery of who this is propels the narrative of the book. It is a good story, but it is possible to see what is coming before it is revealed in the book. Also, Laurie is a little unbelievable in that she figures out some things easily and then appears totally clueless at other times. Actually, I liked the atmosphere of the setting more than anything else. Her house sounds fabulous and the scenery of the cliffs with the waves pounding the rocks is beautifully described. The fact that the kids take a ferry to school on the mainland is kind of neat. I can see why it would have been a good book for teens back when it was written, but I'm not sure how well it would go over with them now. If you are looking for a quick read in the young adult genre this would be a good choice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14466856029357347573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1352483870?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather Moyes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather Moyes" href="/user/show/39906655-heather-moyes">Heather Moyes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352483870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6123631345947530797">WOW I never realised when I'd read it before in my teens, just how dated this book is LOL.<br/>I mean you can tell Lois Duncan was old. I assume the way it's written is much like how she would talk... old fashioned midwest USA. My mother in law is American, grown and raised in Indiana, she talks the same way this was written 'I go with him' 'write me' 'now listen here' etc LOL<br/>I almost expected to read an 'oh boy!' and 'hot diggidy dog!' like my husband's Grandma would say lol.<br/>Anyway, other than the s</span>
  <span id="freeText6123631345947530797" style="display:none">WOW I never realised when I'd read it before in my teens, just how dated this book is LOL.<br />I mean you can tell Lois Duncan was old. I assume the way it's written is much like how she would talk... old fashioned midwest USA. My mother in law is American, grown and raised in Indiana, she talks the same way this was written 'I go with him' 'write me' 'now listen here' etc LOL<br />I almost expected to read an 'oh boy!' and 'hot diggidy dog!' like my husband's Grandma would say lol.<br />Anyway, other than the style of writing, it's still a pretty good book. A great story that can be entertaining to a variety of ages.<br />I was surprised to read that a lot of reviewers had to read this in school. I can't imagine why a school would read this book to be honest. In the UK, we had to read books such as The Hobbit, The Crucible, Of Mice and Men, Lord of the Flies etc in school... I'm really not sure what kids could learn from this book.<br />I'd still recommend reading this with the warning that it seems it's meant to be set in the 50's or something, which is not what I pictured when I was a teenager, as I said, I didn't notice how dated it was at all back then, weirdly.<br />It is fun to read a book you've already read 25 years earlier. Not only does your memory come back about the book, but I also started to remember things in my life back then too, I don't know if that happens to anyone else but it was a nice little trip down memory lane for me :)<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888361391?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/544126-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888361391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11521205694416205185">This book is young adult so I must keep that in mind with my review. I read it as a teenager and remembered it being one of my absolute favorites. Its kind of suspenseful and mysterious. But rereading as an adult I was thoroughly disappointed. I had considered giving it to my teenage niece since I remembered loving it so but I definitely won't now. Maybe its a product of the 80's but there is way too much teenage shallowness and focus on body image and judging - not a positive influence for a te</span>
  <span id="freeText11521205694416205185" style="display:none">This book is young adult so I must keep that in mind with my review. I read it as a teenager and remembered it being one of my absolute favorites. Its kind of suspenseful and mysterious. But rereading as an adult I was thoroughly disappointed. I had considered giving it to my teenage niece since I remembered loving it so but I definitely won't now. Maybe its a product of the 80's but there is way too much teenage shallowness and focus on body image and judging - not a positive influence for a teenage girl. There is also some supernatural abilities attributed to being Navajo. I felt it was inappropriate to assign such a quality to a people and culture that isn't based on reality. Not responsible to do in a book for a teenager. <br /><br />Its a fast easy read but its juvenile. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11521205694416205185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vYs+xriICnQS/oOd8DwW6P4VcXeJOiK04ldG+io/iGQ9mx92AdsOaTIAnzkx2YYpE9IzqSLP+aTw0z5FEp3Tbw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7ldxo5M2DPsXAGzvhdPGBnL6ITtW74l9YNPfMQknmJVuR1ATKmUI5jf+cEtENlbHnz1j5f0aUm1yV6eOMYXDng==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">About Lois Duncan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1197061058p3/26819.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">Lois Duncan
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,603
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2014822142311738835">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz) was an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but grew up in Saraso</span>
  <span id="freeText2014822142311738835" style="display:none">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz) was an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but grew up in Sarasota, Florida. Duncan started writing and submitting manuscripts to magazines at the age of ten, and when she was thirteen succeeded in selling her first story.<br /><br />Duncan attended Duke University from 1952 to 1953 but dropped out, married, and started a family. During this time, she continued to write and publish magazine articles; over the course of her career, she has published more than 300 articles, in magazines such as Ladies' Home Journal, Redbook, McCall's, Good Housekeeping, and Reader's Digest. After her first marriage, which produced three children, ended in divorce, Duncan moved to Albuquerque, New Mexico, to teach journalism at the University of New Mexico, where she also earned a BA in English in 1977. In 1965 she married Don Arquette, and had two more children with him.<br /><br />Duncan was best known for her novels of suspense for teenagers. Some of her works have been adapted for the screen, the most famous example being the 1997 film I Know What You Did Last Summer, adapted from her novel of the same title. Other made-for-TV movies include Stranger with My Face, Killing Mr. Griffin, Don't Look Behind You, Summer of Fear and Gallows Hill.<br /><br />In 1989 the youngest of Duncan's children, Kaitlyn Arquette, was murdered in Albuquerque, New Mexico, under suspicious circumstances. Who Killed My Daughter? relates the facts and conjecture about the still unsolved case. <br /><br />Duncan's second book about her daughter's murder, ONE TO THE WOLVES: ON THE TRAIL OF A KILLER, picks up where the first book leaves off and contains all the new information Kait's family has uncovered from private investigation. <br /><br />The 1971 children's book Hotel for Dogs was released as a theatrical movie in 2009, starring Emma Roberts. That book has now been republished by Scholastic along with two sequels, News for Dogs (2009) and Movie for Dogs (2010).<br /><br />Duncan's Gothic suspense novel, DOWN A DARK HALL, is being filmed for the Big Screen and will probably be released in 2016.<br /><br /><br />Follow Lois on Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/duncanauthor">http://twitter.com/duncanauthor</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=100000216477747&amp;ref=profile">http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?i...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com">http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2014822142311738835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
